#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Colorectal Cancer Detection Using Targeted Serum Metabolic Profiling
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Colorectal cancer (CRC) is one of the most prevalent and deadly cancers in the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Despite an expanding knowledge of its molecular pathogenesis during the past
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	decades, robust biomarkers to enable screening, surveillance, and therapy
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of CRC are still lacking. In this study, we present a targeted liquid
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	mass spectrometry-based metabolic profiling approach for identifying biomarker
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	that could enable highly sensitive and specific CRC detection using human serum
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	In this targeted approach, 158 metabolites from 25 metabolic pathways of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	significance were monitored in 234 serum samples from three groups of patients
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	CRC patients, 76 polyp patients, and 92 healthy controls). Partial least
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	analysis (PLS-DA) models were established, which proved to be powerful for
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	CRC patients from both healthy controls and polyp patients. Receiver operating
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	curves generated based on these PLS-DA models showed high sensitivities (0.96
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	0.89, respectively, for differentiating CRC patients from healthy controls or
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	patients); good specificities (0.80 and 0.88), and excellent areas under the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	(0.93 and 0.95) were also obtained. Monte Carlo cross validation (MCCV) was
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	applied, demonstrating the robust diagnostic power of this metabolic profiling
PR:INSTITUTE                     	University of Washington
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Anesthesiology and Pain Medicine
PR:LABORATORY                    	Northwest Metabolomics Research Center
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Gu
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Haiwei
PR:ADDRESS                       	850 Republican St.
PR:EMAIL                         	haiwei@uw.edu
PR:PHONE                         	7654919481
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	AMRMC grant W81XWH-10-1- 0540, The China Scholarship Council is also gratefully
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	(Grant to L.D.).
PR:PUBLICATIONS                  	Colorectal Cancer Detection Using Targeted Serum Metabolic Profiling, J.
PR:PUBLICATIONS                  	Res., 2014, 13, 4120-4130
#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Colorectal Cancer Detection Using Targeted Serum Metabolic Profiling
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Colorectal cancer (CRC) is one of the most prevalent and deadly cancers in the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Despite an expanding knowledge of its molecular pathogenesis during the past
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	decades, robust biomarkers to enable screening, surveillance, and therapy
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of CRC are still lacking. In this study, we present a targeted liquid
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	mass spectrometry-based metabolic profiling approach for identifying biomarker
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	that could enable highly sensitive and specific CRC detection using human serum
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	In this targeted approach, 158 metabolites from 25 metabolic pathways of
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	significance were monitored in 234 serum samples from three groups of patients
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	CRC patients, 76 polyp patients, and 92 healthy controls). Partial least
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	analysis (PLS-DA) models were established, which proved to be powerful for
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	CRC patients from both healthy controls and polyp patients. Receiver operating
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	curves generated based on these PLS-DA models showed high sensitivities (0.96
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	0.89, respectively, for differentiating CRC patients from healthy controls or
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	patients); good specificities (0.80 and 0.88), and excellent areas under the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	(0.93 and 0.95) were also obtained. Monte Carlo cross validation (MCCV) was
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	applied, demonstrating the robust diagnostic power of this metabolic profiling
